[{"id":27858,"date":"2022-03-31T14:01:13","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T06:01:13","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/?p=27858"},"modified":"2024-01-29T11:59:07","modified_gmt":"2024-01-29T03:59:07","slug":"sustainable-cities-might-be-the-key-to-achieving-the-uns-goals-heres-how-one-waste-to-wonderland-story-is-inspiring-sustainability-across-asia","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/sustainable-cities-might-be-the-key-to-achieving-the-uns-goals-heres-how-one-waste-to-wonderland-story-is-inspiring-sustainability-across-asia\/","title":{"rendered":"Sustainable Cities Might Be the Key To Achieving the UN\u2019s Goals. Here\u2019s How One Waste-to-Wonderland Story Is Inspiring Sustainability Across Asia"},"content":{"rendered":"
    \n
  • \n
    The United Nations has set out 17 goals for building a more sustainable future.<\/h5>\n<\/li>\n
  • \n
    These include promoting sustainable technologies, green innovation, and education for all.<\/h5>\n<\/li>\n
  • \n
    Sunway City Kuala Lumpur in Malaysia is a center for advancing national progress on the goals.<\/h5>\n<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n

    The United Nations’ Sustainable Development Goals are a blueprint for achieving a better and more sustainable future for everyone. From eliminating hunger and investing in healthcare to tackling the climate crisis and ensuring economic growth, the 17 goals \u2014 designed to be achieved by 2030 \u2014 act as a road map for nations, cities, and organizations around the world.<\/p>\n

    The Sustainable Development Solutions Network has been tasked with advancing global progress on the goals: Its national and regional networks are spread across the globe to connect with local countries and territories. SDSN Malaysia was established in 2013, and Sunway City Kuala Lumpur is central to its work.<\/p>\n

    “Addressing the issues related to planetary health and sustainable development is no longer an option but an urgent imperative,” said Tan Sri Sir Jeffrey Cheah, the chairman and founder of Malaysia’s Sunway Group. “We are convinced that the health of the planet and its people are an interconnected and interdependent ecosystem.”<\/p>\n

    Historically, Malaysia’s challenge has been finding equilibrium between growth, universal economic benefit, and preservation of its lush natural environment. It’s a difficult balancing act; Malaysia ranked 56th out of 61 countries in this year’s Climate Change Performance Index.<\/p>\n

    But things are set to change. The number of constituents in the FTSE4Good Bursa Malaysia Index, which measures the performance of public listed companies demonstrating environmental, social, and governance practices, has more than tripled, to 75 from 24, since 2014, while Malaysia this year rose two spots, to 25th, in the International Institute for Management Development’s World Competitiveness Ranking. Kuala Lumpur is on track to become a world-class sustainable city by 2026, the Malaysian Institute of Planners said in 2019, and Sunway City Kuala Lumpur is leading the way.<\/p>\n

    A purpose-built town within Malaysia’s capital is a model for sustainable urban environments<\/h2>\n

    At the heart of this gradual transformation is Sunway City Kuala Lumpur. This thriving, purpose-built town is home to thousands of people from all walks of life. The area is a hotbed of sustainable development, innovation, and learning that’s both shaping an enviable template for sustainable cities worldwide and helping coordinate SDG activities throughout Asia.<\/p>\n

    Sunway City Kuala Lumpur is the flagship of three sustainable towns developed by Cheah’s Sunway Group, one of Southeast Asia’s leading conglomerates. The others are Sunway City Ipoh, in the northern state of Perak, and Sunway City Iskandar Puteri, in southern Malaysia. Sunway City Kuala Lumpur was developed with SDG goals in mind. “This is a reflection of Sunway’s full embrace of the sustainability agenda and our commitment to advancing the SDGs in the Asian region,” Cheah says.<\/p>\n

    The site \u2014 the first to be recognized as a green integrated township by Malaysia’s Green Building Index and as a low-carbon city by Malaysia’s Ministry of Environment and Water \u2014 was built on land ravaged by 1990s tin mining. Cheah had the vision for the development after growing up in a small town where he “witnessed firsthand the impact of poverty on families and how it closed off avenues of advancement,” he said.<\/p>\n

    Cheah’s ethos, “do well by doing good,” has underpinned every stage of the city’s growth. Almost 50% of the 800-acre city is open space, and 24% is green space, with more than 30,000 trees and 150 species of flora and fauna. Buildings are equipped with solar panels, and an elevated highway was designed for electric buses that shuttle Sunway City’s 200,000-plus population between shops, schools, leisure outlets, offices, and a medical center. A water-treatment plant takes advantage of Malaysia’s wet climate to process some 8.5 million liters of water a day, while the smart cloud and the Internet of Things take care of energy consumption, security, and smart parking to ensure optimum efficiency.<\/p>\n

    The development has ambitious plans, too, aiming to be carbon neutral by 2050.<\/p>\n

    Education is a crucial part of the sustainability picture<\/h2>\n

    But sustainability isn’t just about greenery and the environment \u2014 it’s about looking at the bigger picture of poverty, inequality, housing, and healthcare. To ensure that tomorrow’s cities are truly sustainable, learners today need to be equipped with the right skills and knowledge to promote sustainable development. This is the objective of Mission 4.7, the global initiative championing SDG 4.7 (which refers to education and the knowledge and skills needed to promote sustainable development), co-chaired by Cheah.<\/p>\n

    As such, a primary focus in Sunway City Kuala Lumpur is sustainability education, something Cheah believes should be “high-quality, affordable, and accessible” to all. Sunway University, owned by the Jeffrey Cheah Foundation, hosts the Jeffrey Sachs Center on Sustainable Development. (Sachs is a special advisor to the UN secretary-general and the former director of the Earth Institute at Columbia University.) The center is now one of the world’s five SDG Centers of Excellence, and researchers are drawing up a curriculum on sustainable development to be introduced as a compulsory subject for K-12 students around the world.<\/p>\n

    Meanwhile, tech incubation projects like Sunway’s iLabs initiative and the wider GKL Live Lab program are helping attract enterprise to Sunway City Kuala Lumpur, nurturing innovation, solving sustainability challenges, and, importantly, attracting fresh investment, proving that a sustainable city powers itself in more ways than one.<\/p>\n

    These initiatives provide a template for sustainable cities not just in Asia but beyond, with Sunway’s wasteland-to-wonderland success story positioning Sunway City Kuala Lumpur as an inspirational center of living and learning. As Cheah noted in his Mission 4.7 launch speech: “Advancing the SDGs is not the sole responsibility of the governments alone. It requires the commitment of all sectors of society \u2014 the private sector, academia, civil society, and every individual. We are all in this together.”<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"

name=search_term_string"}],"inLanguage":"en-US"},{"@type":"Organization","@id":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/#organization","name":"Sunway","url":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/","logo":{"@type":"ImageObject","inLanguage":"en-US","@id":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/#\/schema\/logo\/image\/","url":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/footer-logo.png","contentUrl":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/footer-logo.png","width":264,"height":40,"caption":"Sunway"},"image":{"@id":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/#\/schema\/logo\/image\/"},"sameAs":["https:\/\/www.facebook.com\/SunwayGroupOfficial\/","https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/SunwayGroupOfficial\/","https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/company\/sunway-group\/","https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/channel\/UCm79RrCIOJ50ZeFAJBeEhFA"]}]}},"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/241"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=241"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}]]}},{"id":25413,"date":"2022-01-12T15:33:38","date_gmt":"2022-01-12T07:33:38","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/?p=25413"},"modified":"2023-11-06T12:59:00","modified_gmt":"2023-11-06T04:59:00","slug":"a-matter-of-corporate-survival-in-post-pandemic-world","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/a-matter-of-corporate-survival-in-post-pandemic-world\/","title":{"rendered":"A Matter Of Corporate \u2018Survival\u2019 In Post-pandemic World"},"content":{"rendered":"<ul>\n<li>\n<h5>Sunway to implement internal carbon pricing in emission reduction push<\/h5>\n<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p>As an early adopter of the sustainable business model, the Sunway Group is ready to ramp up climate action by implementing an internal carbon pricing system to encourage emission reduction across the group.<\/p>\n<p>Sunway has committed to achieving net zero emissions by 2050. It is aiming to gradually cut its carbon footprint each year, in line with the quantum suggested by the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change to lower greenhouse gas emissions by 45% from 2010 levels by 2030.<\/p>\n<p>Putting a price on carbon emissions is a strategy to propel the group forward by tying executive remunerations to the goal, Ong Pang Yen, executive director at the chairman\u2019s office, says in an interview.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are asking all our business units: Look, what is your carbon emission cap, what should be the fair emission in the industry? For our malls, hospitals and office buildings, we\u2019ll take the best benchmark possible and set an emission cap for all the business units,\u201d he adds.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cEven for our quarry, we will ask them, how much CO2 are you producing per tonne? We\u2019ll set the cap based on industry benchmarks and if you emit more than that, you\u2019d have to pay for it. It will affect your pay and bonus.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The COVID-19 crisis has intensified the global call to prepare for future pandemics and mitigate risks arising from climate change. This has pushed more economies around the world to firm up plans to reduce greenhouse gas emissions while stepping up sustainability efforts based on environment, social and governance (ESG) criteria.<\/p>\n<p>In this part of the world, Malaysia has pledged to become a carbon-neutral country by 2050 at the earliest, while neighbouring Indonesia is targeting net-zero emissions by 2060 and Thailand is aiming to achieve the same goal by 2065 to 2070. Singapore has said it will achieve net-zero emissions as soon as viable in the second half of the century.<\/p>\n<p>While many Asian companies may be just beginning to pay more attention to sustainability, Sunway has been a constituent of the FTSE4Good Bursa Malaysia Index for six consecutive years.<\/p>\n<p>Still, Ong says ESG is beyond mere disclosure and numbers to the group. The Group\u2019s sustainability journey reflects its value system and business philosophy, and a lot of this stems from the vision of its founder and chairman Tan Sri Sir Jeffrey Cheah.<\/p>\n<div id=\"attachment_25418\" style=\"width: 1210px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-25418\" class=\"size-full wp-image-25418\" urban environment and skyscrapers from the EcoWalk\" width=\"1200\" height=\"630\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-25418\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The Canopy Walk at Sunway City Kuala Lumpur promotes walkability. It is one of the many examples of the Group\u2019s commitment to a sustainable business model.<\/p><\/div>\n<blockquote><p>\u201cWe are always told that we can do well by doing good. We can do good business by fulfilling the needs of society.\u201d ~ Mr. Ong Pang Yen, executive director of chairman\u2019s office<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Ong says that Cheah turned down the offer of a casino licence a couple of times over the past decade despite the appeal a casino would add to the integrated township developments Sunway is known for.<\/p>\n<p>Cheah\u2019s vision also led him to build the Group\u2019s healthcare division years ago. The healthcare business has matured over the years and is now contributing to the Group\u2019s earnings.<\/p>\n<div id=\"attachment_25447\" style=\"width: 1210px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-25447\" class=\"wp-image-25447 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Facade-of-Sunway-Medical-Centre-featuring-patient-in-wheelchair-and-doctors.jpg\" alt=\"Facade of Sunway Medical Centre featuring patient in wheelchair and doctors\" width=\"1200\" height=\"800\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-25447\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Building a better, healthier nation for all.<\/p><\/div>\n<p>Building assisted living facilities to fulfil the needs of Malaysia\u2019s ageing population and using urban farming to address the food security issues arising from climate change are two other sustainability-related areas where Cheah spotted business opportunities.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are always told that we can do well by doing good. We can do good business by fulfilling the needs of society,\u201d Ong states.<\/p>\n<p>Cheah has earned a reputation for building the Sunway Group by rehabilitating abandoned tin mining land and turning it into a sprawling township over the decades. Sunway\u2019s long-lasting success \u2014 the Group will be celebrating its 50th anniversary in two years\u2019 time \u2014 is a testament to the fact that sustainability pays off in the long term, Ong elaborates.<\/p>\n<p>The Group\u2019s ability to remain profitable and continue paying dividends during the COVID-19 pandemic despite the fact that its key business segments of hospitality and leisure are among the hardest hit during the crisis is another proof that sustainable business does not necessarily come at the cost of profit, according to Ong.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cSustainability and survival are two sides of the same coin. You also have to look at it from the survival point of view. The world is changing, the climate changes, demand for equality is increasing. If you ignore this and don\u2019t prepare well, you may certainly be caught in a tsunami of demands that you may not be able to handle. You\u2019d collapse. So there are also a lot of risks to survival,\u201d he adds.<\/p>\n<div id=\"attachment_25424\" style=\"width: 1210px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img decoding=\"async\" 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-25424\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Sunway\u2019s urban farm helps address food security issues arising from climate change<\/p><\/div>\n<div id=\"attachment_25421\" style=\"width: 1210px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-25421\" class=\"wp-image-25421 id=\"caption-attachment-25421\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The Sunway South Quay Water Treatment Plant. Sunway has committed to achieving net zero emissions by 2050.<\/p><\/div>\n<p>To be sure, not all of Sunway\u2019s business segments are sustainable and friendly to the earth. Ong says that concerns have been raised about its quarry operations. \u201cSome industries are more challenging because they are net emitters of carbon.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cQuarry products are a necessity and somebody will have to do it. We need infrastructure and we need to build. We can\u2019t deny the need for quarry products because that would be a hypocrisy. But we can manage the quarry in the most efficient manner so that it reduces the impact on the environment.\u201d<\/p>\n<p class=\"specialcoverage\"><em>The article originally appeared in <\/em><a in it for the long haul\u201d The Cambridge institute taking on COVID-19"},"content":{"rendered":"<ul>\r\n<li>\r\n<h5>In late 2019, a new institute opened on the Cambridge Biomedical Campus.<\/h5>\r\n<\/li>\r\n<li>\r\n<h5>Its timing could not have been better – as the COVID-19 pandemic sent Britain into lockdown several months later, the institute found itself at the heart of the University\u2019s response to this unprecedented challenge.<\/h5>\r\n<\/li>\r\n<\/ul>\r\n<p>When I first meet Professor Ken Smith in his new office, out of instinct we go to shake hands. There\u2019s an awkward moment as we remember the public health advice and stop ourselves, opting for \u2018elbow bumps\u2019 instead.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>It\u2019s 10th March 2020 and I’m at the\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.citiid.cam.ac.uk\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Cambridge Institute of Therapeutic Immunology and Infectious Disease<\/a>\u00a0(CITIID), which opened in autumn 2019 in the Jeffrey Cheah Biomedical Centre with Smith at its Director. We are meeting to discuss his upcoming\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.nature.com\/articles\/s41586-020-2265-1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><em>Nature\u00a0<\/em>paper<\/a>, the first major publication from the institute, which looks at a rare immune disorder known as primary immunodeficiency.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<div id=\"attachment_10803\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-10803\" class=\"wp-image-10803\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/Ken-Smith-CITIID-1024x640-1.jpeg\" alt=\"\u201cWe're in it for the long haul\u201d The Cambridge institute taking on COVID-19\" width=\"1024\" height=\"640\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-10803\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Professor Ken Smith (Credit: Nick Saffell)<\/p><\/div>\r\n<p>Less than a fortnight later, Britain entered lockdown as SARS-CoV-2 swept the country. Although I didn\u2019t realise it at the time, CITIID would become the last University building I would enter for over three months.<\/p>\r\n<p><!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph --><\/p>\r\n<p><!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph --><\/p>\r\n<p>By the time I return, the Jeffrey Cheah building \u2013 and, indeed, the world \u2013 is a very different place. The bustle on the ground floor has gone \u2013 there are far fewer people around and the caf\u00e9 is closed. Hand sanitiser dispensers greet you at the entrance and signs on the walls remind you to keep your distance. Stickers in the lift tell you where to stand and that only two people should ride at any one time.<\/p>\r\n<p><!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph --><\/p>\r\n<p>But beyond the visible transformation, something fundamental has changed.<\/p>\r\n<p><!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph --><\/p>\r\n<p>CITIID was one of the few University buildings to remain open throughout lockdown. That\u2019s because, as it became clear the world was facing an unprecedented threat, Smith realised that his team had vital expertise that could help fight the pandemic.<\/p>\r\n<p><!-- \/wp:paragraph --><\/p>\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-8621\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/JCBCphoto-1-1024x538-1.jpg\" alt=\"The Jeffrey Cheah Biomedical Centre. Cambridge University Biomedical Centre\" width=\"1024\" height=\"538\" \/><\/p>\r\n<p><!-- wp:quote --><\/p>\r\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\">\r\n<p>\u201cWe realised we had an institute that was quite consciously set up to deal with this sort of thing,\u201d says Smith. He had intentionally recruited people with interests including immunology, inflammation, infectious disease, virology, cell biology, global health, pathogen surveillance… \u201cWe’ve got this broad range of expertise that allows us to look at the problem from all angles.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<\/blockquote>\r\n<p><!-- \/wp:quote -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph --><\/p>\r\n<p>Smith estimates that the institute was running at about 50% capacity, with around 150 scientists, including some from labs elsewhere that had gone into lockdown, but whose work was relevant to the pandemic. Some 60% of the institute\u2019s group leaders also work at one of the hospitals on the\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/cambridge-biomedical.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Cambridge Biomedical Campus<\/a>, including Addenbrooke\u2019s Hospital, part of Cambridge University Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust (CUH).<\/p>\r\n<p><!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph --><\/p>\r\n<p>In fact, while CITIID may have been at the heart of the University’s response from a biomedical perspective, it\u2019s been a hugely collaborative effort, with scientists from all across the Campus \u2013 from other University departments, the Cancer Research UK Cambridge Institute and the Medical Research Council\u2019s Laboratory for Molecular Biology pulling together to fight COVID-19.<\/p>\r\n<p> <\/p>\r\n<p class=\"specialcoverage\"><em>The article originally appeared in <\/em><a href=\"https:\/\/www.cam.ac.uk\/stories\/citiid\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">University of Cambridge’s Stories<\/a><\/p>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<div class='heateorSssClear'><\/div><div class='heateor_sss_sharing_container City Kuala Lumpur: Sustainable and Smart Through Technology"},"content":{"rendered":"<ul>\r\n<li>\r\n<h5>Sunway Group is tapping the cloud and other advanced technologies to add an array of smart capabilities to Malaysia\u2019s first fully integrated green township.<\/h5>\r\n<\/li>\r\n<\/ul>\r\n<p>Four decades ago, Malaysia\u2019s\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.sunway.city\/main.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Sunway City Kuala Lumpur<\/a>\u00a0was little more than a wasteland, barren and virtually devoid of life following years of mining upheaval. Gravel, sand, and mud were essentially all that was left behind.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Today, the\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/building-a-smart-and-sustainable-future\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">800-acre site<\/a>\u00a0is Malaysia\u2019s first fully integrated green township, serving a vibrant community of more than 200,000 people with smart energy management systems, an elevated electric bus system, free Wi-Fi, and an array of sustainability features that have earned it numerous certifications and awards. Green space makes up roughly 40% of the township, which is now home to more than 150 species of flora and fauna. Coexisting among them are an award-winning mall, a water theme park, three hotels, multiple universities, a medical center, and residential and commercial buildings, all accessible via interlinked, elevated pedestrian walkways emphasizing low-carbon connectivity within the township.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:image -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter\" title=\"...\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/2020-09-25_12-27-41.png\" alt=\"Sunway City Kuala Lumpur: Sustainable and Smart Through Technology\" width=\"1169\" height=\"503\" \/><\/p>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>But plans for Sunway City Kuala Lumpur don\u2019t end there. The result of a massive restoration and rehabilitation effort by Sunway Group, one of Malaysia\u2019s largest conglomerates, Sunway City Kuala Lumpur is now undergoing another transformation. Using Google Cloud and other advanced technologies, the company is working to make the township a model smart, sustainable city as well.<\/p>\r\n<blockquote>\r\n<div id=\"attachment_14377\" style=\"width: 190px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-14377\" class=\"wp-image-14377\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/Tan-Sri-Dato-Chew-Chee-Kin-Group-President-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"180\" height=\"164\" srcset=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/Tan-Sri-Dato-Chew-Chee-Kin-Group-President-1-200x182.jpg 200w, https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/Tan-Sri-Dato-Chew-Chee-Kin-Group-President-1-230x209.jpg 230w, https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/Tan-Sri-Dato-Chew-Chee-Kin-Group-President-1.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 180px) 100vw, 180px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-14377\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Tan Sri (Dr.) Chew Chee Kin, Sunway Group\u2019s president<\/p><\/div>\r\n<p>For many years, Sunway has been promoting and advocating the idea of a smart, sustainable township, a concept that encompasses a holistic vision that goes beyond just \u2018going green\u2019 and reducing carbon footprints,\u201d says Tan Sri (Dr.) Chew Chee Kin, Sunway Group\u2019s president. \u201cWe hope that our journey to becoming a smart and sustainable city will create a ripple effect that encourages citizens to participate in creating a better future for all.<\/p>\r\n<\/blockquote>\r\n<h2>Driven by Data in the Cloud<\/h2>\r\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>At the heart of Sunway\u2019s newest transformation effort was the realization that it needed a single source of truth for its data in order to deliver the intended customer experience. Working with Google Cloud and Deloitte, it has begun work to consolidate the data from across many of its 13 business units while using predictive analytics to better understand its customers.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:quote -->\r\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\">\r\n<div id=\"attachment_10682\" style=\"width: 190px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-10682\" class=\"wp-image-10682\" title=\"Kevin Khoo...\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/Kevin.jpg\" alt=\"Kevin Khoo\" width=\"180\" height=\"180\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-10682\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Kevin Khoo<\/p><\/div>\r\n<p>\u201cBy putting our information in Google Cloud, we\u2019re becoming a data-driven organization and gaining better insight into new opportunities,\u201d says Kevin Khoo, Sunway\u2019s Group CIO.<\/p>\r\n<p> <\/p>\r\n<\/blockquote>\r\n<!-- \/wp:quote -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Enabling those opportunities, meanwhile, are an array of advanced technologies. Examples include smart parking, cashless payments, smart energy management, and an AI-driven, centralized security system. \u201cIf there\u2019s a problem somewhere, it will be possible for emergency services to be deployed automatically,\u201d Khoo says. Plans call for Sunway City Kuala Lumpur to become fully\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/deloitte.wsj.com\/cio\/2020\/01\/24\/5g-build-it-and-they-will-come\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">5G-enabled<\/a>, further\u00a0powering the township\u2019s surveillance system as well as new capabilities such as augmented and virtual reality technology that enables citizens to experience the thrills of Sunway City Kuala Lumpur\u2019s theme park from home.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>In the Sunway Pyramid Mall, a \u201cmagic mirror\u201d will enable customers to try on clothes virtually; coupled with\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/deloitte.wsj.com\/cio\/2020\/07\/21\/thriving-in-the-era-of-pervasive-ai\/\">AI<\/a>, it could even make recommendations for complementary accessories. \u201cThe AI can recognize the shopper\u2019s gender and recommend a size,\u201d explains Chew. \u201cThis will be especially valuable given the pandemic, since customers are not able to try on clothes in person.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:quote -->\r\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\">\r\n<p>“We hope that our journey to becoming a smart and sustainable city will create a ripple effect that encourages citizens to participate in creating a better future for all.”<\/p>\r\n<cite><em>\u2014Tan Sri (Dr.) Chew Chee Kin, president, Sunway Group<\/em><\/cite><\/blockquote>\r\n<!-- \/wp:quote -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Plans for enhanced remote education are also in the works, tapping facial recognition and AI, while blockchain technology will be used to ensure the transparency and authenticity of academic certificates delivered to university students. To improve internal processes in the township, robotic process automation technologies such as software robots will automate mundane and repeatable tasks. Expanded telehealth capabilities will include medicine delivery via drone. Sunway City Kuala Lumpur also plans to deploy a fleet of autonomous buses.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:heading -->\r\n<h2>\u2018There\u2019s No Limit\u2019<\/h2>\r\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Ultimately, much of the new innovation being launched in Sunway City Kuala Lumpur will likely find its way into other Sunway townships throughout Malaysia as well. In the meantime, Sunway continues to look toward the future. Aiming to foster entrepreneurship and drive innovation, for example, its Sunway iLabs initiative offers an accelerator program that can provide funding and mentorship as well as connect start-ups to Sunway\u2019s business units as a test bed for technologies and business models. Meanwhile, 42KL, a nonprofit tech education initiative, uses project-based and peer-to-peer learning to help build a world-class digital talent pool.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph --><!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>42KL in Sunway City Kuala Lumpur is one of the first such efforts in Southeast Asia; Sunway envisions it as a sort of living laboratory \u2014an open ecosystem where research and innovation can take place within a \u201cpublic-private-people\u201d partnership.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<div id=\"attachment_10446\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-10446\" class=\"wp-image-10446\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/42KL-1024x536-2.jpg\" alt=\"42KL Coding School\" width=\"1024\" height=\"536\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-10446\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">42KL presents peer-to-peer learning approach, doing away with traditional classrooms, teachers and tuition fees.<\/p><\/div>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>With an eye toward sustainability in the years ahead, Sunway will soon launch Sunway FutureX, a skills-building hub to help urban farming professionals, tech companies, researchers, and budding entrepreneurs collaborate and create transformative solutions focusing on food and agritech.\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/deloitte.wsj.com\/cio\/2018\/07\/26\/5-tech-advances-propel-iot\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Internet of things<\/a>\u00a0technologies will play a central role.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph --><!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-10467 aligncenter\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/10\/FutureX-Building-Closeup-1024x669-1.jpg\" alt=\"Sunway FutureX\" width=\"1024\" height=\"669\" \/><\/p>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Though the term \u201csmart city\u201d is relatively new, the idea isn’t, says Chew. \u201cSince the start of the development of our first township, we have been working to enhance the living standards of our community,\u201d he says. \u201cWith the right talent, partners, and technologies, there\u2019s no limit to what\u2019s possible.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><em>\u2014by\u00a0<\/em><a href=\"https:\/\/deloitte.wsj.com\/cio\/about-deloitte-insights\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"><em>Katherine Noyes<\/em><\/a><em>, senior writer, Deloitte Insights for CIOs<\/em><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph University as \u2018the Harvard or Cambridge of the East\u2019.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>\u201cI am aware this is unlikely to be realised in my lifetime, but what I am doing is setting the foundation stones to realise my aspirations for the future. Slowly, but surely, we will get there,\u201d he opined.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The immediate milestone he is eyeing is for the university to number among the global top 100 institutions in the coming decade, but that\u2019s not all. Cheah is also actively advocating to empower private universities to operate via the university endowment model.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Endowment funds, sourced from donations and then invested for returns, enable universities to operate in perpetuity by helping maintain academic excellence, advance research and development, cover operating expenses and wages, as well as provide financial aid for deserving students among others.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>For instance, the University of Cambridge, United Kingdom, has an endowment of \u00a36.90bil (RM36.91bil), while Harvard University, United States, has US$40.90bil (RM174.38bil).<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Some may say that it is a pipe dream, but the same was said for Sunway City Kuala Lumpur. Similarly, it had its share of naysayers that – as Cheah recalled – labelled him \u2018crazy\u2019 for buying a piece of barren wasteland \u2018full of holes\u2019 located in Sungai Way in 1986 with the intention of rehabilitating it into a sustainable and vibrant township.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>In line with the 17 United Nations Sustainable Development Goals (UN SDG) – which Cheah deeply espouses, as evidenced by the establishment of the Jeffrey Sachs Centre on Sustainable Development (JSC) at Sunway University – work is still underway to improve the township through deeper integration of technology to establish it as a model smart sustainable city.<br \/><br \/>Towards this goal, Sunway recently partnered with Celcom and Huawei in a tripartite collaboration towards advancing smart township solutions encompassing the Internet of Things and artificial intelligence with fifth-generation (5G) connectivity. The Memorandum of Understanding aims to explore the potential for Celcom and Huawei to be the 5G technology enabler for Sunway Group, while Sunway City KL will be the \u2018launch pad\u2019 for the groundbreaking partnership.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<div id=\"attachment_7571\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-7571\" class=\"wp-image-7571\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/08\/Tan-Sri-Dr-Jeffrey-Cheah-at-Teach-for-Malysia-2-1024x538-1.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1024\" height=\"538\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-7571\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Cheah (standing, right) believes that education is the best way to combat poverty.<\/p><\/div>\r\n<!-- wp:heading -->\r\n<h2>Striving for the best<\/h2>\r\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The journey of Sunway University thus far is marked by tremendous growth. According to the QS World University Rankings by Subject 2020, Sunway University – despite its relative youth – ranks among the top 500 universities in the world for its business and management studies discipline.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Such recognition reflects the strength of the academic institution\u2019s reputation.<br \/><br \/>When Cheah started the education institution in 1987, then known as Sunway College, it was hard to imagine that a Malaysian academic institution could compete with the best universities globally.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>But it has certainly made its mark, pushing the envelope in education through the years. For instance, it was a pioneer of the twinning programme concept. At the time, the country was in recession and parents could not afford higher education for their children overseas, which was when Cheah came up with the concept.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Cheah also set up the education-focused not-for-profit Jeffrey Cheah Foundation (JCF), to which he transferred the equity and rights of Sunway Education Group\u2019s (SEG) educational institutions worth several billion ringgit into the foundation in perpetuity.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The foundation owns and governs all 16 educational institutions and entities under the SEG, including Sunway University and has awarded more than RM482mil in scholarships and grants to date. It is Cheah\u2019s personal goal to award more than RM1bil in his lifetime.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>He said, \u201cWhat we want to do is provide a helping hand rather than hand-outs and I believe the best way to do so is through education. \u201cJCF has come a long way since it was established 10 years ago. And I believe its structure of managing SEG\u2019s operation surpluses and administering it into scholarships and grants will further benefit the education and sustainability sphere towards nation building.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Today, it has active partnerships with prestigious academic institutions such as the University of Cambridge, Harvard University, the University of Oxford and the Massachusetts Institute of Technology among others, which are certainly not easy feats by any measure.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>It has also sealed collaborative partnerships with Cambridge in the form of the Jeffrey Cheah Biomedical Centre, which is considered the centrepiece of the largest biotechnology cluster outside the United States, as well as the Sunway-Cambridge joint Clinical Research Centre that will serve as Cambridge\u2019s regional site partner, the first such venture of its kind for Cambridge.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>\u201cSunway University is relatively young, but to be able to gain the recognition and to collaborate with these renowned institutions itself speaks volumes on our quality and dedication,\u201d he opined.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Aside from working with the best academic institutions in the world, another instance that demonstrates Cheah\u2019s conviction in learning from the best is the appointment of the Jeffrey Cheah distinguished professors.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>He explained, \u201cThese professors are very accomplished in their own fields and they do not easily lend their name to any institutions. For them to be affiliated with Sunway University shows how much trust and confidence they have in us and our not-for-profit model.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<div id=\"attachment_10261\" style=\"width: 782px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-10261\" class=\"wp-image-10261\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/The-Star-19-July-2020_03.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"772\" height=\"515\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-10261\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Being able to gain the recognition of renowned institutions such as Oxford is proof of Sunway University\u2019s quality, says Cheah (right).<\/p><\/div>\r\n<div id=\"attachment_10262\" style=\"width: 1010px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-10262\" class=\"wp-image-10262\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/The-Star-19-July-2020_04.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1000\" height=\"487\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-10262\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Cheah points in the direction of the Sunway Medical Centre, with Sunway Lagoon in the background.<\/p><\/div>\r\n<!-- wp:heading -->\r\n<h2>Aspiring to inspire<\/h2>\r\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>As JCF celebrates its 10th anniversary, it is a proud moment for Cheah, who stuck to his goal to provide quality education to students despite the fact that it was loss-making for 12 years.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The reason for this tenacity can be traced back to Cheah\u2019s formative years in Pusing, Perak, where he witnessed first-hand the impact of poverty on families and how it closed off avenues for advancement for children.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>\u201cEducation is particularly close to my heart. Very early on, I became convinced that education offers the best route out of poverty and misery. I stayed the course, even when my senior managers advised me to get out of the sector because the losses were hurting our company then.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>\u201cI believed that by setting up the college and admitting students, I had made a promise to our children and it was a pledge I was determined to keep,\u201d he shared.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Moreover, Cheah has also contributed much to philanthropic efforts over the years. He is the only Malaysian who has been named three times on Forbes Asia\u2019s annual definitive philanthropy list, Heroes of Philanthropy.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>This proves that for Cheah, entrepreneurship, philanthropy and even education are all means to an end: towards nation-building and creating a sustainable future for all.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The most important thing, he said, is to identify the end goal and then plan the journey to achieve that goal accordingly – but before that, he stressed on first having the ability to achieve wealth through entrepreneurship with the right values.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>He said, \u201cAfter all, you need to make money first before you can give it out.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>\u201cPersonally for me, what I want is to build a sustainable future for the next generation to continue to excel and contribute to a progressive and prosperous society. Entrepreneurship, quality education, philanthropy and sustainability are the avenues towards reaching my goal.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Cheah, who above all aspires to inspire before he \u2018expires\u2019, added, \u201cI hope what we\u2019re doing at Sunway will inspire other corporations and individuals in this part of the world to do more. We can all do well by doing good.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:heading -->\r\n<h2>Setting the bar in education<\/h2>\r\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Cheah\u2019s belief in working with the best and learning from the best also birthed the appointments of the Jeffrey Cheah distinguished professors.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Under the collaboration between Jeffrey Cheah Foundation and globally acclaimed academic institutions, eminent experts and scholars – who have contributed to solving critical global issues in health, disease and economy amongst others – are appointed to share their knowledge and expertise with Malaysian academics, students and the general public.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:heading -->\r\n<h2>Among the prominent names on the list are:<\/h2>\r\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-10275 alignnone\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-Jeffrey-David-Sachs-731x1024-1.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"366\" height=\"512\" \/><\/p>\r\n<p><strong>Prof Jeffrey David Sachs<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<p>As a world renowned economist and director of the UN Sustainable Development Solutions Network, Prof Sachs is one of the world\u2019s most influential experts on sustainable economic development.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>A passionate leader in the fight against poverty and the special advisor to the UN secretary-general on sustainable development, he has advised heads of states and governments on economic strategy for more than a quarter century.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Appointed as an honorary Jeffrey Cheah distinguished professor of sustainable development at Sunway University this year, he is also the chairman of the Jeffrey Sachs Centre on Sustainable Development.<\/p>\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-10264\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-Sir-Leszek-Borysiewicz-FRS.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1000\" height=\"668\" \/><\/p>\r\n<p><strong>Prof Sir Leszek Borysiewicz<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The chairman of Cancer Research United Kingdom (UK) since 2016, Prof Borysiewicz is an Honorary Jeffrey Cheah distinguished professor who is now the emeritus vice-chancellor of the University of Cambridge, after serving as its vice-chancellor from 2011 to 2017.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>A founding fellow of the Academy of Medical Sciences, he has been chief executive of the UK\u2019s Medical Research Council since 2007 and was knighted in 2001 for his breakthroughs in vaccines, including developing Europe\u2019s first trial of a vaccine to treat cervical cancer.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-10274\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-Sir-Alan-Fersht-FRS_01.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1000\" height=\"668\" \/><\/p>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><strong>Prof Sir Alan Fersht<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>World leading protein scientist Prof Fersht, also an honorary Jeffrey Cheah distinguished professor and life fellow of Gonville and Caius College Cambridge, is widely regarded as one of the main pioneers of protein engineering, which is a process to analyse the structure, activity and folding of proteins.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>His current research involves a fusion of protein engineering, structural biology, biophysics and chemistry to study the structure, activity, stability and folding of proteins, as well as the role of protein misfolding and instability in cancer and disease.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-10269\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-Kay-Tee-Khaw-CBE_01.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1000\" height=\"668\" \/><\/p>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><strong>Prof Kay-Tee Khaw<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Prof Khaw, a leading expert in the field of health and disease, is a Jeffrey Cheah professorial fellow in Gonville and Caius College, Cambridge. She is currently one of the principal UK scientists working on the European Prospective Investigation into Cancer and Nutrition, a Europe-wide project investigating the links between diet, lifestyle and cancer.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Appointed as a Commander of the order of the British Empire in 2003, Prof Khaw has been recognised for developing improved methods for collecting information on people\u2019s diets and levels of exercise and relating this to the number of diagnosed cancer cases.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-10272\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-Rema-Hanna_01.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1000\" height=\"668\" \/><\/p>\r\n<p><strong>Prof Rema Hanna<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>A highly distinguished economist, Prof Hanna is the Jeffrey Cheah professor of South East Asia Studies and chair of the Harvard Kennedy School International Development Area, as well as the faculty director of evidence for policy design at Harvard\u2019s Centre for International Development and the co-scientific director of the Abdul Latif Jameel Poverty Action Lab South East Asia office in Indonesia.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Her focus is on improving overall service delivery, understanding the impacts of corruption, bureaucratic absenteeism and discrimination against disadvantaged minority groups on delivery outcomes.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-10270 alignnone\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-KJ-Patel-FRS_01-683x1024-1.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"342\" height=\"512\" \/><\/p>\r\n<p><strong>Prof Ketan J Patel<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Prof Patel is a Jeffrey Cheah professorial fellow in Gonville and Caius College, Cambridge and the principal research scientist at the famous MRC Laboratory of Molecular Biology in the University of Cambridge.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>His research, which focuses on the molecular basis of inherited genomic instability and the role it plays in the biology of stem cells, has been recognised through prestigious awards and prizes, including being elected as a fellow of the Royal Society of London, a member of the European Molecular Biology Organisation and a fellow of the Academy of Medical Sciences UK.<\/p>\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-10271\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-Mark-Wilson_01.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1000\" height=\"668\" \/><\/p>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><strong>Prof Mark Wilson<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Prof Wilson, the dean of Brasenose College, is a Jeffrey Cheah professorial fellow at the college and the professor of physical chemistry in the University of Oxford\u2019s physical and theoretical chemistry department.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The primary focus of his research interest is on the construction, development and application of relatively simple potential models to assess a wide range of systems with potentially unique properties.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-10268\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-John-Todd-FRS_01.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1000\" height=\"668\" \/><\/p>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><strong>Prof John Todd<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The Jeffrey Cheah fellow in medicine at Brasenose College, Oxford and professor of precision medicine, Prof Todd is a leading pioneer researcher in the fields of genetics, immunology and diabetes. His research areas include Type 1 diabetes genetics and disease mechanisms with the aim of clinical intervention.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>In his former role as a professor of human genetics and a Wellcome Trust principal research fellow at Oxford, he helped pioneer genome-wide genetic studies, first in mice and then in humans.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-10267 alignnone\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-Jarlath-Ronayne-AM_01-683x1024-1.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"342\" height=\"512\" \/><\/p>\r\n<p><strong>Prof Jarlath Ronayne<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<p>Appointed in 2010 as the first Jeffrey Cheah distinguished professor, Prof Ronayne is a key member of Sunway University\u2019s board of directors and has played a pivotal role in establishing links between Sunway, Oxford and Cambridge.<\/p>\r\n<p>Under his leadership, the Jeffrey Cheah Professorial Fellowships at Gonville and Caius College, Cambridge as well as Brasenose College, Oxford and the Jeffrey Cheah Scholar-in-Residence programmes in both colleges were established, alongside the prestigious Oxford University-Jeffrey Cheah Graduate Scholarship launched by the British High Commissioner in 2018. All these initiatives are in perpetuity.<\/p>\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-10329 alignnone\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-William-Swadling_01.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"450\" height=\"656\" \/><\/p>\r\n<p><strong>Prof William Swadling<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<p>Prof Swadling, a Jeffrey Cheah professorial fellow, is a senior law fellow at Brasenose College, Oxford and Professor in the Law of Property in the Oxford University Law School.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>An expert on the Law of Restitution, he is a contributor to Halsbury\u2019s Laws of England, wrote the section on property in Burrows (ed) English Private Law and is widely cited in the British courts.<\/p>\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-10265\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-William-James.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"1000\" height=\"659\" \/><\/p>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><strong>Prof William James<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>A Jeffrey Cheah professorial fellow emeritus and fellow in medicine at Brasenose College, Oxford, Prof James is a virologist with a background in genetics and microbiology.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>As the professor of virology with the University of Oxford, he is the principal investigator at the Stem Cell Research Institute of Oxford, running a research lab studying HIV-macrophage biology using stem cell technology.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-10273 alignnone\" src=\"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/07\/Professor-Sibrandes-Poppema_01-731x1024-1.jpg\" alt=\"Leaving a legacy to inspire\" width=\"366\" height=\"512\" \/><\/p>\r\n<p><strong>Prof Sibrandes Poppema<\/strong><\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>A medical expert on Hodgkin\u2019s disease, Prof Poppema has published more than 200 articles that have been cited more than 17,000 times.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The Jeffrey Cheah distinguished professor is also the co-owner of 12 patents and the founder of two biotechnology companies, as well as the advisor to the chancellor at Sunway University, especially on the establishment of a new medical school at the university.<\/p>\r\n<p> <\/p>\r\n<p class=\"specialcoverage\"><em>The article originally appeared in <\/em><a Good","publisher":{"@id":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/#organization"},"potentialAction":[{"@type":"SearchAction","target":{"@type":"EntryPoint","urlTemplate":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/?s={search_term_string}"},"query-input":"required name=search_term_string"}],"inLanguage":"en-US"},{"@type":"Organization","@id":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/#organization","name":"Sunway","url":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/","logo":{"@type":"ImageObject","inLanguage":"en-US","@id":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/#\/schema\/logo\/image\/","url":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/footer-logo.png","contentUrl":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/footer-logo.png","width":264,"height":40,"caption":"Sunway"},"image":{"@id":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/#\/schema\/logo\/image\/"},"sameAs":["https:\/\/www.facebook.com\/SunwayGroupOfficial\/","https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/SunwayGroupOfficial\/","https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/company\/sunway-group\/","https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/channel\/UCm79RrCIOJ50ZeFAJBeEhFA"]}]}},"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/36"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=36"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}]]}},{"id":9775,"date":"2020-06-09T11:32:55","date_gmt":"2020-06-09T03:32:55","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/?p=9775"},"modified":"2023-11-06T10:39:10","modified_gmt":"2023-11-06T02:39:10","slug":"quo-vadis-the-post-pandemic-world","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/www.naqibtech.com\/stories\/quo-vadis-the-post-pandemic-world\/","title":{"rendered":"\u201cQuo vadis\u201d the post-pandemic world?"},"content":{"rendered":"<p>On 11 March 2020, the World Health Organisation declared COVID-19 as a global pandemic. It was merely an official acknowledgement of the reality that nations and populations were already experiencing.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Suddenly, the world came to a shuddering stop as the focus shifted, rightly, to combating the virus and saving lives.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>There is little need for me to go into great detail here about the threat posed by this pathogen to our lives and its impact on economic livelihoods.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Instead, I would like to focus on the fundamental question of where do we go from here?<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>As the world takes frantic steps to recover from this devastating body blow, will it be a return to \u201cbusiness as usual\u201d \u2014 as what happened following the 2007-2008 financial crisis \u2014 or will we use the occasion of this \u201cpause\u201d to hit the \u201creset\u201d button?<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Will we have the will and the courage to take the necessary decisions and steps to build a future that is just, progressive and sustainable for our future generation?<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Or are we tied to a\u00a0future of rising income inequality, widening wealth disparities, polarised societies, sick and starving populations, dangerous geopolitical tensions, and an ailing planet.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>I am an optimist by nature. Even in these deeply pessimistic times, I strongly believe that humanity will rise to the challenges that confront us, and that we can navigate our way to a better tomorrow.\u00a0<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Let\u2019s start with our current\u00a0economic system. Over the last 200 years, the world has enjoyed tremendous economic growth. This progress and prosperity are remarkable, but they have come at an enormous cost.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>We are now struggling to cope with the environmental, social and governance problems that growth has brought in its wake. The COVID-19 pandemic has starkly exposed many of these shortcomings.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The reasons for how we have come to be where we are today are many. But I believe a major factor is our obsession with unbridled growth, as measured by the metric known as Gross Domestic Product (GDP).<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>GDP has come to be perceived as a proxy for the wealth of a nation. But while GDP may arguably be effective in measuring the standard of living, it largely falls short in valuing the quality of life.\u00a0<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>We need a wider lens to measure how we are doing. We need metrics that reflect our well-being as nations, communities and individuals, not just a GDP number which bears little relation to every day reality.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>In the words of Professor Kate Raworth of Oxford University\u2019s Environmental Change Institute and author of the influential book \u201cDoughnut Economics\u201d: Instead of economies that need to grow, whether or not they make us thrive, we need economies that make us thrive, whether or not they grow.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Her views offer a conceptual framework that prioritises people and shifts the focus to quality of life, with economic growth being a means toward those ends.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The good news is, the path towards this transformation has already been charted for us. On 25th September 2015, the\u202f193 members of the United Nations General Assembly adopted the UN 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development. The resolution calls for action through long-term development pathways comprising 17 Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs). These goals serve as a comprehensive and holistic global vision towards development that seeks to heal the socio-economic and environmental ills afflicting the world.\u202f<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>A crucial aspect of the SDGs is their interconnectivity, and their emphasis on the human condition. For instance, many tend to think \u201cclimate change\u201d when they hear the term sustainable development. However, it is noteworthy that the first five SDGs \u2013 no poverty, zero hunger, good health and well-being, quality education and gender equality \u2013 prioritise people.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Despite world-wide adoption, the SDGs are still largely perceived to be aspirational. Their implementation by nations varies by wide degrees and is limited by our economic and financial structures, and mindsets.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The COVID-19 crisis offers a genuine opportunity to address these limitations and to advance the sustainability agenda through the SDGs. The United Nations Sustainable Development Solutions Network (SDSN) is formulating several avenues through which to channel these efforts.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>One of these key initiatives is for the SDG Academy, an online knowledge network, to draw up a curriculum on sustainable development to be mandated as a compulsory subject at K-12 levels around the world. Another is to set up three overarching SDSN centres to coordinate continent-wide sustainability initiatives. These centres will be located in New York City (North and South America); Paris (Europe and Africa); and Sunway City Kuala Lumpur (Asia).<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>These plans were scheduled to be announced by Pope Francis at the Vatican\u00a0on 14 May.\u00a0That announcement has now been re-scheduled for October because of the pandemic.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n<blockquote>\r\n<p>I mean a (compassionate) capitalist system that<br \/>motivates and incentivises us to do well by doing good \u2013 one that shifts the focus to People, Planet, Prosperity.<\/p>\r\n<\/blockquote>\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>I am particularly proud that Sunway University, where the SDSN centre for\u00a0Asia will be housed, has been chosen as an important player in this global effort. It reflects Sunway\u2019s embrace of the sustainability agenda and our commitment to advancing the SDGs in the Asian region.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The necessity of such efforts, at both practical and policy levels, takes on greater urgency in the wake of the pandemic and its threat to lives and livelihoods.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The impact of COVID-19 on public finances all over the world, with even governments led by neoliberal ideologues ramping up massive deficits, and on the bottom lines of corporations clearly implies the need for a change.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>The very ethos of the capitalist system that has dominated the past four decades is now under increasing scrutiny.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>I welcome such initiatives. I am an entrepreneur, and a firm supporter of capitalism and the efficacy of markets. But I submit that\u00a0to build a better tomorrow, we must seize the opportunity to move beyond what some have called \u201ccowboy capitalism\u201d towards \u201ccompassionate capitalism.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>To put it simply, I mean a capitalist system that motivates and incentivises us to do well by doing good \u2014 one that shifts the focus from the quarterly bottom-line of profits to the \u201cThree P\u201d bottom-line of People, Planet, Prosperity by taking into account the interests of all stakeholders.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>This will entail a more balanced approach on determining the roles of the market and the state. Indeed, over and above systemic change, it requires\u00a0a shift in societal values.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Perhaps this is best encapsulated in the remark by Mahatma Gandhi \u201cThe\u202f world has enough for everyone’s needs, but not everyone’s greed.\u201d<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>In the wake of the pandemic, fulfilling everyone\u2019s needs requires us to take a piercing look at ourselves as individuals, and as a society. It calls for us to emphasise values such as compassion, empathy, tolerance and inclusiveness.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>It demands more equitable outcomes in policy-making by governments and market operations by the private sector.\u00a0<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>And in keeping with Gandhi\u2019s words, it means a system and values that place the highest priority on societal needs and curbs individual greed.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>Systemic change and a shift in values represent an immense challenge to humanity. Are we \u2014\u00a0as individuals, families, communities and nations \u2014 prepared to \u201creset\u201d our future?<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\r\n<p>I believe we are, we can, and we must. We are all in this together.<\/p>\r\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\r\n\r\n<!-- wp:quote -->\r\n<blockquote>\r\n<p><em>Tan Sri Sir Jeffrey Cheah is founder and chairman of Sunway Group, one of Malaysia\u2019s largest conglomerates, and founder and trustee of the Jeffrey Cheah Foundation. He is also a member of the global Leadership Council of the UN Sustainable Development Solutions Network (SDSN) and chairman of its Malaysian chapter.<\/em><\/p>\r\n<\/blockquote>\r\n<!-- \/wp:quote
